ثم لقائل أن يقول إن الحرارة مثلاً وحدها لا تكون ضدا بل تكون بالقياس إلى البرودة وحينئذ تكون مضافة فإنها وإن لم تكن من حيث هي حرارة من المضاف. فلا تكون أيضًا بمضادة فهي إذن من حيث هي ضد ماهية مقولة بالقياس إلى الغير فتكون مضافة. ثم التضاد والتضايف إما شيء واحد أو التضاد شيء داخل تحت التضايف فلا يكون كالقسم له تحت التقابل. وهنا شبهة أخرى وهي أن التقابل من حيث هو التقابل من المضاف؛ ثم المضاف تحته وأخص منه هذا خلف. لكنا نقول الحرارة ينظر إليها وإلى البرودة معا؛ فالحرارة من حيث هي حرارة ضد للبرودة. ثم يؤخذ من حيث هو ضد مرة أخرى فتكون مضافة إلى البرودة فتكون الحرارة بنفس اعتبارها مع البرودة يصح عليهما معنى الضد بالحقيقة : ولا يصح عليهما معنى المضاف؛ إذ ليس أحدهما مقول الماهية بالقياس إلى الآخر. فإذن الموضوع في حمل الضدية شيء، والموضوع في حمل الإضافة شيء، وذلك إما نفس المحمول الأول أو مجموع الموضوع والمحمول، فالموضوع المضادة إذا أخذت مضادة صارت سبب ذلك مضافة ولا ينعكس، فالتضاد إذن غير التضايف. وأما الشبهة / الأخرى فيجب أن تعلم أن المتقابلات تعرض لها الإضافة [م٧١و] وليست هي في هويتها بمضافات. فإن كل تقابل من حيث هو تقابل مضاف؛ وليس كل تقابل بمضاف. وفُرقَ بينهما لما أن التضاد من التقابل؛ وقد علم أن الموضوع له ليس هو الموضوع للمضاف كما مرَّ لكن الموضوع من حيث هو تقابل يصير موضوع المضاف ; فلذلك ليست الأمور المتضادة مقولة الماهية بالقياس إلا أن يقال من حيث هي متضادة وليست الملكة والعدم من المضاف أيضًا. ولو كان المضاف أمرًا مقولاً على التقابل قولا مطلقا فلا وجود للمتقابلين إلا وأن يكونا متضايفين مطلقًا لا شرط إلحاق أنهما كذلك: وليس كذلك فإن كل متضايف متقابل ، ولا ينعكس؛ فلا يمكن أن يكون المتضايف أعم من التقابل، ولا المتضايف إذن من التقابل. ثم التقابل ليس جنسًا لما تحته بوجه من الوجوه؛ وذلك لأن المتضايف ماهيته أنه مقول بالقياس إلى الغير، ثم يلحق هذه الماهية أن يكون مقابلة ليست أنها متقومة بهذا. وكيف هو ولا يجب أن يتقدم في الذهن أو لا حتى
Then an objector may say that heat alone, for example, is not a contrary, but becomes so relative to cold, and then it becomes a relative. For even if it is not from its being heat among the relatives, it is also not by way of contrariety. So it is from its being a contrary a quiddity said relative to another, so it becomes a relative. Then contrariety and correlativity are either one thing or contrariety is included under correlativity, so it is not a division of it under opposition. And here is another doubt: that opposition from the perspective of being opposition is among the relatives; then the relative is under it and more specific than it, this is a contradiction. But we say: heat is considered along with cold together; heat from its being heat is a contrary to cold. Then it is taken from its being a contrary once again, so it becomes a relative to cold. So heat, in the very consideration with cold, the meaning of contrary truly applies to both; but the meaning of relative does not apply to both, since neither is a quiddity said with reference to the other. Thus the subject in the predication of contrariety is something, and the subject in the predication of relativity is something else. That is either the first predicate itself or the sum of subject and predicate. So the subject of contrariety, when taken as contrary, becomes the cause of that relativity, and it does not reflect. Therefore contrariety is not correlativity. As for the other doubt, you must know that opposites are accidentally relative and are not in their essence relatives. For every opposition from the perspective of being opposition is relative, but not every opposite is a relative. A distinction is made between them because contrariety is part of opposition; and it is known that the subject for it is not the subject for the relative, as has passed, but the subject from the perspective of being opposition becomes a subject for the relative. Therefore contrary things are not quiddities said with reference, except if they are said from the perspective of being contrary. And possession and privation are also not relatives. If the relative were said absolutely about opposition, then there would be no existence of opposites except as they are correlatives absolutely, without the condition of attaching that they are so. But it is not so, for every correlative is an opposite, but not every opposite is a correlative. So it is impossible for the correlative to be more general than opposition, nor is the correlative from opposition. Then opposition is not a genus for what is under it in any way; because the correlative's quiddity is that it is said with reference to another, then this quiddity is attached that it is opposite, not that it is constituted by this. And how is it and it does not have to precede in the mind or not even...
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage presents a dialectical exchange: an objector claims that contrariety (taddad) and correlativity (tadāyuf) are either identical or that contrariety is subsumed under correlativity, because a contrary like heat becomes relative when considered with its opposite. The objector also raises a doubt that opposition itself is relative, so the relative would be under it, leading to a contradiction. The author refutes this by analysing heat and cold: as heat, it is a contrary to cold; when taken as a contrary, it accrues relationality but not essentially. The subject of 'contrary' is different from the subject of 'relative'; in contrariety, the quiddities are not said essentially with reference to each other. Thus contrariety is not the same as correlativity. The second doubt is addressed by noting that opposites can accidentally acquire relationality but are not essentially relatives. Every correlative is an opposite, but not vice versa, so correlativity is not more general. Finally, opposition is not a genus for its species because the essence of a relative (being said with reference to another) is prior, and opposition is an accidental attribute that attaches to it, not constituting it. The argument shows that taqabul (opposition) is a broader category with distinct species, and tadāyuf and taddad are not reducible to each other.

التضايف
المضاف

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is heat not a relative (mudaf) in the same way that it is a contrary?
A) Because heat is a quality, not a relation
B) Because the meaning of relative does not apply to both heat and cold, since neither is a quiddity said essentially with reference to the other
C) Because heat and cold are not opposites
D) Because heat is only relative when separated from cold

Key Takeaway
Contrariety and correlativity are distinct logical categories: contraries are opposed in themselves with accidental relation, while correlatives are essentially defined by mutual reference.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Write how a mutakallim would respond using the author's distinction between essential and accidental relation.
?

Distinguishing Taqabul's Species: Contrariety, Correlativity, and Others
Author refutes objection equating contrariety and correlativity, clarifying their distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why contrariety is not a subtype of correlativity, and identify the correct relationship between taqabul, tadad, and tadayuf.

Core Idea
Opposition is broader than correlativity: every correlative is an opposite, but not every opposite is a correlative.

This passage not only refutes an objection but also establishes the proper logical hierarchy between opposition (taqabul), contrariety (tadad), and correlativity (tadayuf). The author argues that opposition is not a genus for its species in the strict sense, but a broader category. We will dissect these definitions and their relationships.

Guided Path
1
Extract the definitions of tadad and tadayuf
From the passage and key terms, note: tadad (contrariety) is between two opposites like heat and cold; the quiddities are not essentially relative but become so accidentally. Tadayuf (correlativity) applies to things whose quiddities are essentially said with reference to each other, like father and son.
These definitions are standard in post-Avicennan logic.
2
Analyze the objector's claim that tadad is under tadayuf
The objector reasons: heat alone is not a contrary, but becomes so relative to cold; therefore contraries are relations, so tadad is a species of tadayuf. The author refutes by showing that the subject of tadad is the quiddity itself, not the relation.
The key is that in tadad, the quiddity is not defined by relation; in tadayuf, it is.
3
Understand the claim that 'every correlative is an opposite, but not every opposite is a correlative'
The author asserts this to show that tadayuf is a proper species of taqabul, not the other way around. This is because correlatives are inherently opposite (they are mutually opposed in reference), but opposites like contraries or possession-privation are not essentially relations.
This is a logical mistake to think that because tadad involves comparison, it is a relation.
4
Examine why taqabul is not a genus
The author says taqabul is not a genus for what is under it because the quiddity of a relative (being said with reference to another) is prior, and being opposite is an accidental attachment, not constitutive. A true genus must be part of the quiddity of its species.
This is a subtle point: taqabul is a broader category but not a genus in the sense of having a shared differentia.

Distinguishing Contrariety from Correlation
Author refutes a doubt by distinguishing contrariety from correlation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish contrariety (tadadd) from correlation (tadāyuf) by testing whether the terms are essentially relative to each other.

Core Idea
Contraries are not essentially relative; correlatives are.

A doubt arises: perhaps all opposition is merely relative. The author responds by examining heat and cold, a pair of contraries. He shows that while they are related, neither is defined by the other, unlike true correlatives such as father and son. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion between categories of opposition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the doubt
The doubt claims that opposition (taqabul) as such belongs to the category of relation (mudāf). That would mean every pair of opposites are correlatives.
2
Examine the example: heat and cold
Heat is a contrary of cold. But is heat essentially predicated of cold? No. Heat is not the essence of cold, nor is cold the essence of heat.
In correlation, each term is essentially relative: father is father of son, and son is son of father.
3
Apply the test of essential predication
Check whether one term is predicated of the other in the category of essence (maqul al-mahiyya). For heat and cold, neither is. Therefore they are not correlatives.
Correlatives satisfy the condition that each is defined by reference to the other.
4
Distinguish the subjects of predication
The subject in 'heat is contrary to cold' differs from the subject in 'heat is relative to cold'. The latter adds the relation as a secondary connotation, not the primary meaning.
Contrariety can be a cause for relation, but not the other way around.
5
Conclude that contrariety is distinct from correlation
Since the logical structure differs, contrariety (tadadd) is not a subset of correlation (tadāyuf). They are two independent types of opposition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبهة أخرى وهي أن التقابل من حيث هو التقابل من المضاف؛ ثم المضاف تحته وأخص منه هذا خلف. لكنا نقول الحرارة ينظر إليها وإلى البرودة معا؛ فالحرارة من حيث هي حرارة ضد للبرودة. ثم يؤخذ من حيث هو ضد مرة أخرى فتكون مضافة إلى البرودة فتكون الحرارة بنفس اعتبارها مع البرودة يصح عليهما معنى الضد بالحقيقة : ولا يصح عليهما معنى المضاف؛ إذ ليس أحدهما مقول الماهية بالقياس إلى الآخر. فإذن الموضوع في حمل الضدية شيء، والموضوع في حمل الإضافة شيء، وذلك إما نفس المحمول الأول أو مجموع الموضوع والمحمول، فالموضوع المضادة إذا أخذت مضادة صارت سبب ذلك مضافة ولا ينعكس، فالتضاد إذن غير التضايف.
Another doubt: that opposition, as it is opposition, is relative; then the relative is under it, and more specific than it, this is contradictory. But we say: heat is considered along with cold; heat is a contrary of cold. Then it is taken as contrary once again, so it becomes relative to cold. So heat, by the same consideration with cold, the meaning of contrary truly applies to them, and the meaning of relative does not apply to them, because neither of them is a predicate of the essence in relation to the other. Therefore, the subject in the predication of contrariety is something, and the subject in the predication of relation is something else, and that is either the first predicate itself or the totality of subject and predicate. So the subject of contrariety, if taken as contrary, becomes the cause of that relation, and not vice versa. Thus contrariety is not correlation.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage begins with a doubt: that opposition (taqabul) as such belongs to the category of relation (mudāf). The author refutes this by considering heat and cold. Heat is a contrary of cold, but heat is not essentially predicated of cold, nor vice versa. In correlation (tadāyuf), each term is predicated of the other essentially (e.g., father and son). Therefore, contrariety is not the same as correlation. The author explains that the subject in the predication of contrariety is different from the subject in the predication of relation, and the relation is a consequence of the contrariety, not the definition.

Why Opposition is Not a Genus
Author explains opposition as relative but not all opposites are correlatives, and opposition is not a genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between opposition as a relative property and the essence of opposites, and explain why opposition cannot be a genus.

Core Idea
Opposition is a concomitant attribute, not a genus — it does not constitute the essence of its species.

In this passage from the logic text, the author tackles a subtle objection: is opposition essentially a relation? He argues that while every opposition involves a relation, opposites are not defined by that relation. Furthermore, opposition is not a genus that includes contrariety, correlation, and privation/possession as species. Instead, it is a property that accrues to them. Understanding this distinction is crucial for precise definition in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms
Locate the key terms 'opposition' (taqabul) and 'relation' (idafa) in the Arabic. Note that all opposites are in some way relative, but the author claims they are not essentially relatives.
For example, black and white are opposed but each is defined by its own color, not by its relation to the other.
2
Distinguish opposition from relation
The author says 'every opposition as opposition is relative, but not every opposite is relative'. Understand that opposition is a property of the pair, not the essence of each member.
The example of contrariety: heat and cold are opposite, but heat is not defined as 'the non-cold'.
3
Examine why opposition is not a genus
If opposition were a genus, its species (contrariety, correlation, possession/privation) would be defined by opposition. But each species has its own independent essence (e.g., correlatives are defined by relation to another). Opposition is an additional attribute that accompanies them.
The author says: 'the essence of the correlative is that it is predicated in relation to another, then this essence is accompanied by being opposite'.
4
Test the claim
Apply the test: if opposition were a genus, every opposite would be a relative per se, but that is false. For example, black and white are opposites but not essentially relatives; they are defined by their own natures.
Also, every correlative is opposite, but not every opposite is a correlative, so opposition is broader.

وأما الشبهة الأخرى فيجب أن تعلم أن المتقابلات تعرض لها الإضافة وليست هي في هويتها بمضافات. فإن كل تقابل من حيث هو تقابل مضاف؛ وليس كل تقابل بمضاف. وفُرقَ بينهما لما أن التضاد من التقابل؛ وقد علم أن الموضوع له ليس هو الموضوع للمضاف كما مرَّ لكن الموضوع من حيث هو تقابل يصير موضوع المضاف ; فلذلك ليست الأمور المتضادة مقولة الماهية بالقياس إلا أن يقال من حيث هي متضادة وليست الملكة والعدم من المضاف أيضًا. ولو كان المضاف أمرًا مقولاً على التقابل قولا مطلقا فلا وجود للمتقابلين إلا وأن يكونا متضايفين مطلقًا لا شرط إلحاق أنهما كذلك: وليس كذلك فإن كل متضايف متقابل ، ولا ينعكس؛ فلا يمكن أن يكون المتضايف أعم من التقابل، ولا المتضايف إذن من التقابل. ثم التقابل ليس جنسًا لما تحته بوجه من الوجوه; وذلك لأن المتضايف ماهيته أنه مقول بالقياس إلى الغير، ثم يلحق هذه الماهية أن يكون مقابلة ليست أنها متقومة بهذا. وكيف هو ولا يجب أن يتقدم في الذهن أو لا حتى يتقرر ذلك وهو أنه مقول بالقياس إلى الغير بل الأمر على العكس، فإنه إذا صار متضايفا لزم أن يكون على صفة التقابل، والقول بين المفيدة في هذه الأعراض من جملة ما يعرف من بعد في موضعه إن شاء الله تعالى.
As for the other doubt, you should know that opposites occur with relation, but they are not in their essence relatives. For every opposition as opposition is relative; but not every opposition is relative. And the distinction between them is that contrariety is from opposition; and you have known that the subject of the one is not the subject of the relative as mentioned, but the subject as it is opposition becomes the subject of the relative. Therefore, contrary things are not predicated essentially in relation unless it is considered as they are contrary, and privation and possession are also not from the relative. And if the relative were predicated of opposition absolutely, then there would be no existing opposites except that they would be correlatives absolutely without condition that they are so. But it is not so, for every correlative is opposite, but not vice versa; thus the correlative cannot be more general than opposition, nor is opposition from the correlative. Then opposition is not a genus for what is under it in any respect; because the essence of the correlative is that it is predicated in relation to another, then this essence is accompanied by being opposite, not that it is constituted by it. How could it be? It is not necessary that it precede in the mind or not until that is established, namely that it is predicated in relation to another; rather the contrary: when it becomes correlative, it necessarily has the attribute of opposition. And the saying about the useful distinction in these accidents is among what will be known later in its place, God willing.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage addresses another doubt: whether opposition as such is relative. The author explains that while every opposition is relative in a sense, not every opposite is a relative per se. For example, contrariety (tadadd) is a type of opposition, but the subject of contrariety (e.g., heat) is not essentially predicated of the opposite (cold). So the relation is incidental. Then the author argues that opposition is not a genus for its species (contrariety, correlation, privation/possession). The species have their own essences; opposition is a concomitant attribute, not a constitutive genus. The author uses the example of correlation: a correlative is essentially defined by relation to another, but being opposite is an additional attribute that comes later. If opposition were a genus, its species would be essentially defined by opposition, which is not the case.

الملكة والعدم

Why is opposition not a genus for its species according to the author?
A) Because there are only four species of opposition.
B) Because the species have independent essences and opposition is an additional attribute.
C) Because all opposites are essentially relatives.
D) Because opposition is a category, not a genus.

Key Takeaway
Opposition is not a genus; it is a concomitant property that accrues to species with independent essences.

Distinguishing Privation-Possession from Contrariety
Author distinguishes 'adam wa malaka from tadhad with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a pair of opposites belongs to privation-possession or contrariety by checking the conditions of the subject and the possibility of an intermediate.

Core Idea
Privation requires a subject apt to possess; contrariety does not.

The author of this passage carefully distinguishes privation-possession from other types of opposition, especially contrariety. The key difference lies in the condition of the subject: in privation-possession, the subject must be naturally capable of possessing the quality, and the privation occurs only when that quality is absent at a time when it could be present. Contrariety has no such condition; the subject can transition between contraries at any time, and an intermediate state is possible. Let's explore these conditions step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the pair of opposites
Take a pair like sight and blindness (privation-possession) or black and white (contrariety). Determine which type the author is analyzing.
2
Check the subject's aptitude
In privation-possession, the subject must be naturally apt to possess the quality. For example, a human can have sight, so blindness is the privation of sight in a human. But a stone cannot have sight, so blindness does not apply. In contrariety, the subject may or may not have such aptitude.
3
Examine the possibility of an intermediate
In contrariety, an intermediate can exist (e.g., lukewarm between hot and cold). In privation-possession, no intermediate exists: either the quality is present or it is not (e.g., sight or blindness).
The author mentions real vs popular types of privation-possession; in real type one must be present at any time.
4
Check if one opposite is defined by the negation of the other
In privation-possession, the privation is defined as the absence of the possession. In contrariety, one contrary is not necessarily defined as the negation of the other.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الموضوع للمضادة قد يعرض له أن يكون مضافًا، ولا كذلك الموضوع للإضافة على ما عرف. وكذلك بينهما وبين العدم والملكة: فلأن الموضوع في العدم والملكة موضوع واحد من شأن كل واحد منهما أن يكون فيه. ولكن ليس كيف اتفق بل إنما يكون فيه العدم بأن تعدم الملكة في الموضوع وقتا من شأنها أن تكون موجودة فيه للموضوع كما يعدم البصر في الموضوع وقتا من شأنه أن تكون له ملكة البصر. ولا وجود لهذا الشرط في قسمي التضاد فإن الموضوع المشترك للضدين اللذين لا واسطة بينهما يجوز في كل وقت أن ينتقل من أحدهما إلى الآخر، إلا أن يكون طبيعيا لا يفارق كبياض الققتس [؟]. وأيضًا يمكن في المتضادين أن يوجد الوسط دون الطرفين، ولا يمكن في العدم والملكة فإن في الحقيقي منه لا بد من أحدهما وفي المشهوري كذلك في الوقت. وأيضًا لا يلزم أن يكون أحد الضدين بين ارتفاع الآخر بخلاف العدم والملكة. وأما ما يكون بينهما وبين المشهوري على الخصوص أو بين الحقيقي كذلك فذلك يعرف بالتأمل بعد الإطلاق على كل واحد منهما. وكذلك ما يكون بين المتناقضين والمتضايفين فإنه في غاية الظهور بعد الاطلاع على حقيقة كل واحد منهما. وعلى هذا فيما يكون بينهما والعدم والملكة، وفيما يكون بين المتضايفين والعدم والملكة كذلك. واعلم أنا إذا قلنا عدم وملكة أو غير ذلك من المتقابلات فلسنا نشير منها إلا إلى طبائعها لا إليها من حيث وجودها للموضوع أو كون الموضوع متصفاً بها، فليس العمى وأن يعمى فالبصر وأن يبصر شيئًا واحدًا: ولهذا يقال زيد يعمى ولا يقال زيد عمى، وكون العمى لزيد معنى يقتضي نسبته للعمى إلى زيد. وأما العمى فهو معنى مفهوم بنفسه أو بسبب ما عدمه هو أعني البصر؛ إذ هو عدم للبصر، فهذه ليست المتقابلات الأول بل أمور تلحق المتقابلات فيعرض لها أن يكون مقابله. وعلى هذا في السلب والإيجاب فإن ما يوجب أو يُسلب نفسه ليس بقول بل هو محمول في القول كقولك جالس وليس بجالس. ثم العدم والملكة لا يكون أحدهما مقولاً بالنسبة إلى الآخر؛ أما الملكة فليست مفتقرة في تصورها إلى العدم البتة، وأما العدم كالعمى فإنه وإن كان لا يتصور إلا بتصور الملكة فإنه ليس مقول الماهية بالقياس إلى الملكة. وقد ظن بعض الناس أن العمى ينسب إلى البصر من طريق جنسه أو ما هو كجنسه وهو العدم. فإن العدم معقول بالعرض وبسبب ما هو عدمه: وهذا خطأ فإن العدم الذي هو جنس العمى ليس مقول الماهية بالقياس إلى شيء ولا بالقياس إلى الملكة. فإن العدم ليس إنما هو عدم لأجل أنه مقيس إلى صورة موضوعة في الذهن بإزائها يقال له عدم كما يكون العمى عميا لأن الملكة ملكة. وكما يكون الأب أبا لأن الابن ابن فينعكس من الجانبين لما أن القول بالقياس عبارة عن حال الشيء من جهة أن شيئًا آخر موجود بإزائه، ومأخوذ أيضًا من حيث هو كذلك. وليس حال الملكة عند العدم كذلك بل ينسب إليها العدم بإزاء زوالها وفقدانها فقدان شيء آخر كيف اتفق؛ وبهذا يظهر أن العدم والملكة ليسا بمتضايفين. وبالجملة فكما أن بين الفرسية واللا فرسية والسواد والبياض والأبوة والبنوة والعمى والبصر تقابلا فكذلك بين الفرس واللا فرس والأب والابن والأبيض والأسود والأعمى والبصير لكن التقابل الأول وبالذات هو ما ليس فيه الموضوع؛ فإنه إذا أخذ فيه الموضوع كان تقابلا بالقصد الثاني، وبالعرض لا بالذات.
The subject for contrariety may happen to be relative, but not the subject for relation as known. Likewise between them and privation and possession: because the subject in privation and possession is a single subject capable of each of them being in it. But not however, rather possession is absent in it only when the possession is absent from the subject at a time when it is apt to exist in it for the subject, just as sight is absent from the subject at a time when it is apt to have the possession of sight. And this condition does not exist in the two divisions of contrariety, for the common subject of two contraries between which there is no intermediate may at any time transition from one to the other, unless it is natural and not separable, like the whiteness of the cactus [?]. Also, in contraries it is possible for the intermediate to exist without the extremes, but not in privation and possession, for in the real [type] of it one of them is necessary, and in the popular [type] similarly at the time. Also, it is not necessary that one of the contraries be the product of the negation of the other, unlike privation and possession. As for what is between them and the popular specifically, or between the real likewise, that is known by reflection after applying [the term] to each of them. And likewise what is between the contradictories and the relatives, for it is extremely clear after understanding the reality of each of them. And similarly regarding what is between them and privation and possession, and what is between the relatives and privation and possession likewise. Know that when we say privation and possession or other such correlatives, we only refer to their essences, not to them from the aspect of their existence for the subject or the subject's being qualified by them. So blindness and being blind, and sight and seeing are not the same thing: hence it is said 'Zayd becomes blind' and it is not said 'Zayd is blindness'. And the fact that blindness belongs to Zayd is a meaning that necessitates attributing blindness to Zayd. But blindness itself is a meaning conceived by itself or by virtue of what it is the privation of, namely sight, for it is the privation of sight. So these are not the primary correlatives, but things that attach to the correlatives and happen to be opposite. Similarly in negation and affirmation, for what affirms or negates itself is not a statement, but it is a predicate in a statement, like your saying 'sitting' and 'not sitting'. Then privation and possession are such that one of them is not predicated relative to the other. As for possession, it does not depend in its conception on privation at all. As for privation like blindness, although it is not conceived except by conceiving the possession, yet it is not predicated essentially in relation to the possession. Some people have thought that blindness is attributed to sight by way of its genus or what is like its genus, namely privation. For privation is understood accidentally and because of what it is the privation of. This is an error, for the privation that is the genus of blindness is not predicated essentially in relation to anything, nor in relation to the possession. For privation is not privation because it is measured to a form placed in the mind opposite to which it is called privation, just as blindness is blindness because possession is possession. And just as the father is father because the son is son, and it is reciprocal from both sides, because the expression 'in relation' is an expression of the state of a thing from the aspect that another thing exists opposite to it, and it is also taken from that aspect. But the state of possession in relation to privation is not like that; rather, privation is attributed to it in regard to its removal and loss, the loss of something else however. And by this it appears that privation and possession are not relative. In summary, just as there is opposition between horseness and not-horseness, blackness and whiteness, fatherhood and sonship, blindness and sight, similarly between the horse and the not-horse, the father and the son, the white and the black, the blind and the seeing; but the first opposition and essential is that which does not include the subject; for if the subject is included, it is opposition in the second intention, and accidental not essential.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification and definition of the types of opposition (taqabul), focusing on the distinction between 'adam wa malaka (privation and possession) and other types: tadhad (contrariety), idafa (relation), and naqd (contradiction). The author proceeds step by step, clarifying conditions of subject. He begins by noting that the subject of contrariety can sometimes be relative, unlike the subject of relation. Then he compares contrariety with privation-possession: in privation-possession, the subject must be capable of possessing the quality, and the privation occurs when the possession is absent at a time when it could be present. This condition does not hold for contraries, where the subject can transition between them at any time, unless it is a natural inseparable property (like the whiteness of a cactus). Also, contraries can have an intermediate state (e.g., lukewarm between hot and cold), but privation-possession cannot have an intermediate; in the real type of privation-possession (e.g., sight/blindness) one must be present at any given time, and in the popular type (e.g., wealth/poverty) it is time-specific. Moreover, contraries are not necessarily defined by the negation of the other, unlike privation-possession where the privation is defined as the absence of the possession. The author then notes that the distinctions between real and popular types become clear after reflection. Next, he addresses a key ontological point: when we speak of 'adam wa malaka, we refer to the natures themselves, not to their existence in a subject or the subject's being qualified by them. So 'blindness' is not the same as 'being blind'; the latter is a relation to the subject. The former is a concept understood by itself or as the privation of sight. These are not the primary opposites but rather attributes that attach to opposites. Similarly, in affirmation and negation, the predicate itself (e.g., 'sitting') is not a statement but a predicate in a statement. Then he argues that privation and possession are not relative (mutadayif). Possession does not require privation for its conception. Privation requires possession for its conception but is not essentially predicated relative to possession. He refutes the mistaken view that blindness is attributed to sight through its genus (privation). Privation is not a genus that is essentially predicated; it is understood accidentally as the absence of something. Unlike true relatives (e.g., father and son) which are reciprocal and each is defined in relation to the other, privation is merely the removal of possession, not a two-way relation. Finally, he summarizes: opposition exists between natures (e.g., horseness/not-horseness, blackness/whiteness, fatherhood/sonship, blindness/sight) and also between concrete instances (e.g., horse/not-horse, etc.). The primary and essential opposition is that which does not include the subject; when the subject is included, it is opposition in the second intention and accidental.

Key Terms
العدم والملكة
التضاد

Which of the following is a key difference between privation-possession and contrariety?
A) In privation-possession, the subject can transition between opposites at any time.
B) In privation-possession, the privation occurs only when the possession could be present but is absent.
C) In contrariety, an intermediate state is impossible.
D) In contrariety, one opposite is always defined as the negation of the other.

Key Takeaway
Privation-possession is distinguished from contrariety by the condition that the subject must be naturally apt to possess the quality, and the privation is defined as its absence when it could be present.

10 min
Why Privation and Possession Are Not Relative
Author refutes that 'adam wa malaka are relative (mutadayif) and clarifies the misconception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to refute the claim that privation and possession are relative by applying the conditions of reciprocity and essential predication.

Core Idea
Privation cannot be a genus nor a relative; it is accidental absence.

The author goes beyond simply defining privation-possession; he also clarifies its relationship to other types of opposition, especially relative terms (mutadayif). Some mistakenly think that privation (like blindness) is related to possession (like sight) as a genus or as a relative. The author refutes this by showing that possession does not depend on privation for its conception, and the relation is not reciprocal. Let's walk through his argument.

Guided Path
1
Check if one term requires the other for conception
Possession (e.g., sight) can be conceived without any reference to privation. But privation (e.g., blindness) requires conceiving the possession. This is one-way, not reciprocal.
2
Test reciprocity
True relatives are reciprocal: father and son, each defined by the other. In privation-possession, possession is not defined by privation. So the relation is not two-way.
3
Examine essential predication
If privation were a genus, it would be predicated essentially of its species. But privation is not a genuine genus; blindness is not essentially privation, but a specific privation of sight. Privation is understood accidentally as the absence of something.
4
Identify the error in the mistaken view
The author points out that some people think blindness is attributed to sight via the genus 'privation'. He explains that privation is not a genus predicated essentially; it is a relative concept only in the sense of being measured against a form in the mind, but not a true reciprocal relation.

ثم العدم والملكة لا يكون أحدهما مقولاً بالنسبة إلى الآخر؛ أما الملكة فليست مفتقرة في تصورها إلى العدم البتة، وأما العدم كالعمى فإنه وإن كان لا يتصور إلا بتصور الملكة فإنه ليس مقول الماهية بالقياس إلى الملكة. وقد ظن بعض الناس أن العمى ينسب إلى البصر من طريق جنسه أو ما هو كجنسه وهو العدم. فإن العدم معقول بالعرض وبسبب ما هو عدمه: وهذا خطأ فإن العدم الذي هو جنس العمى ليس مقول الماهية بالقياس إلى شيء ولا بالقياس إلى الملكة. فإن العدم ليس إنما هو عدم لأجل أنه مقيس إلى صورة موضوعة في الذهن بإزائها يقال له عدم كما يكون العمى عميا لأن الملكة ملكة. وكما يكون الأب أبا لأن الابن ابن فينعكس من الجانبين لما أن القول بالقياس عبارة عن حال الشيء من جهة أن شيئًا آخر موجود بإزائه، ومأخوذ أيضًا من حيث هو كذلك. وليس حال الملكة عند العدم كذلك بل ينسب إليها العدم بإزاء زوالها وفقدانها فقدان شيء آخر كيف اتفق؛ وبهذا يظهر أن العدم والملكة ليسا بمتضايفين. وبالجملة فكما أن بين الفرسية واللا فرسية والسواد والبياض والأبوة والبنوة والعمى والبصر تقابلا فكذلك بين الفرس واللا فرس والأب والابن والأبيض والأسود والأعمى والبصير لكن التقابل الأول وبالذات هو ما ليس فيه الموضوع؛ فإنه إذا أخذ فيه الموضوع كان تقابلا بالقصد الثاني، وبالعرض لا بالذات.
The subject for contrariety may happen to be relative, but not the subject for relation as known. Likewise between them and privation and possession: because the subject in privation and possession is a single subject capable of each of them being in it. But not however, rather possession is absent in it only when the possession is absent from the subject at a time when it is apt to exist in it for the subject, just as sight is absent from the subject at a time when it is apt to have the possession of sight. And this condition does not exist in the two divisions of contrariety, for the common subject of two contraries between which there is no intermediate may at any time transition from one to the other, unless it is natural and not separable, like the whiteness of the cactus [?]. Also, in contraries it is possible for the intermediate to exist without the extremes, but not in privation and possession, for in the real [type] of it one of them is necessary, and in the popular [type] similarly at the time. Also, it is not necessary that one of the contraries be the product of the negation of the other, unlike privation and possession. As for what is between them and the popular specifically, or between the real likewise, that is known by reflection after applying [the term] to each of them. And likewise what is between the contradictories and the relatives, for it is extremely clear after understanding the reality of each of them. And similarly regarding what is between them and privation and possession, and what is between the relatives and privation and possession likewise. Know that when we say privation and possession or other such correlatives, we only refer to their essences, not to them from the aspect of their existence for the subject or the subject's being qualified by them. So blindness and being blind, and sight and seeing are not the same thing: hence it is said 'Zayd becomes blind' and it is not said 'Zayd is blindness'. And the fact that blindness belongs to Zayd is a meaning that necessitates attributing blindness to Zayd. But blindness itself is a meaning conceived by itself or by virtue of what it is the privation of, namely sight, for it is the privation of sight. So these are not the primary correlatives, but things that attach to the correlatives and happen to be opposite. Similarly in negation and affirmation, for what affirms or negates itself is not a statement, but it is a predicate in a statement, like your saying 'sitting' and 'not sitting'. Then privation and possession are such that one of them is not predicated relative to the other. As for possession, it does not depend in its conception on privation at all. As for privation like blindness, although it is not conceived except by conceiving the possession, yet it is not predicated essentially in relation to the possession. Some people have thought that blindness is attributed to sight by way of its genus or what is like its genus, namely privation. For privation is understood accidentally and because of what it is the privation of. This is an error, for the privation that is the genus of blindness is not predicated essentially in relation to anything, nor in relation to the possession. For privation is not privation because it is measured to a form placed in the mind opposite to which it is called privation, just as blindness is blindness because possession is possession. And just as the father is father because the son is son, and it is reciprocal from both sides, because the expression 'in relation' is an expression of the state of a thing from the aspect that another thing exists opposite to it, and it is also taken from that aspect. But the state of possession in relation to privation is not like that; rather, privation is attributed to it in regard to its removal and loss, the loss of something else however. And by this it appears that privation and possession are not relative. In summary, just as there is opposition between horseness and not-horseness, blackness and whiteness, fatherhood and sonship, blindness and sight, similarly between the horse and the not-horse, the father and the son, the white and the black, the blind and the seeing; but the first opposition and essential is that which does not include the subject; for if the subject is included, it is opposition in the second intention, and accidental not essential.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification and definition of the types of opposition (taqabul), focusing on the distinction between 'adam wa malaka (privation and possession) and other types: tadhad (contrariety), idafa (relation), and naqd (contradiction). The author proceeds step by step, clarifying conditions of subject. He begins by noting that the subject of contrariety can sometimes be relative, unlike the subject of relation. Then he compares contrariety with privation-possession: in privation-possession, the subject must be capable of possessing the quality, and the privation occurs when the possession is absent at a time when it could be present. This condition does not hold for contraries, where the subject can transition between them at any time, unless it is a natural inseparable property (like the whiteness of a cactus). Also, contraries can have an intermediate state (e.g., lukewarm between hot and cold), but privation-possession cannot have an intermediate; in the real type of privation-possession (e.g., sight/blindness) one must be present at any given time, and in the popular type (e.g., wealth/poverty) it is time-specific. Moreover, contraries are not necessarily defined by the negation of the other, unlike privation-possession where the privation is defined as the absence of the possession. The author then notes that the distinctions between real and popular types become clear after reflection. Next, he addresses a key ontological point: when we speak of 'adam wa malaka, we refer to the natures themselves, not to their existence in a subject or the subject's being qualified by them. So 'blindness' is not the same as 'being blind'; the latter is a relation to the subject. The former is a concept understood by itself or as the privation of sight. These are not the primary opposites but rather attributes that attach to opposites. Similarly, in affirmation and negation, the predicate itself (e.g., 'sitting') is not a statement but a predicate in a statement. Then he argues that privation and possession are not relative (mutadayif). Possession does not require privation for its conception. Privation requires possession for its conception but is not essentially predicated relative to possession. He refutes the mistaken view that blindness is attributed to sight through its genus (privation). Privation is not a genus that is essentially predicated; it is understood accidentally as the absence of something. Unlike true relatives (e.g., father and son) which are reciprocal and each is defined in relation to the other, privation is merely the removal of possession, not a two-way relation. Finally, he summarizes: opposition exists between natures (e.g., horseness/not-horseness, blackness/whiteness, fatherhood/sonship, blindness/sight) and also between concrete instances (e.g., horse/not-horse, etc.). The primary and essential opposition is that which does not include the subject; when the subject is included, it is opposition in the second intention and accidental.

Key Terms
العدم والملكة
المتضايفان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are privation and possession not relative according to the author?
A) Because both are defined by each other.
B) Because possession does not require privation for its conception.
C) Because privation is a genus of possession.
D) Because the subject is always included.

Key Takeaway
Privation and possession are not relative because possession is conceived independently, and the relation is one-way and accidental.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Explain why 'knowledge and ignorance' is a privation-possession pair, not a relative pair, using the author's reasoning about conception and reciprocity.

Primary and Secondary Opposition: Subject Included or Not
Author summarizes the essential vs accidental opposition based on whether the subject is included.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between primary (essential) opposition and secondary (accidental) opposition by checking whether the subject is included in the opposing terms.

Core Idea
Primary opposition is between natures, not qualified subjects.

The author concludes the passage by summarizing the types of opposition and introducing a crucial distinction: opposition can be considered either between the natures themselves (e.g., horseness and not-horseness) or between the concrete instances where the subject is included (e.g., horse and not-horse). The first is essential; the second is accidental. This distinction helps us understand the logical structure of opposition more precisely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the pair of natures
Look for abstract terms like 'horseness', 'blackness', 'fatherhood', 'blindness'. These are natures without subjects. The opposition between them is primary and essential.
2
Identify the pair with subject included
When the subject is added, we get concrete terms like 'horse', 'black', 'father', 'blind'. The opposition now involves the subject. This is secondary and accidental.
3
Determine the level of opposition
Primary opposition does not include the subject; secondary does. The author says this is like the difference between first and second intention.
4
Apply to Islamic examples
Take 'knowledge' and 'ignorance' (natures) vs 'knowing person' and 'ignorant person'. The first is essential opposition; the second includes the subject and is accidental.

الموضوع للمضادة قد يعرض له أن يكون مضافًا، ولا كذلك الموضوع للإضافة على ما عرف. وكذلك بينهما وبين العدم والملكة: فلأن الموضوع في العدم والملكة موضوع واحد من شأن كل واحد منهما أن يكون فيه. ولكن ليس كيف اتفق بل إنما يكون فيه العدم بأن تعدم الملكة في الموضوع وقتا من شأنها أن تكون موجودة فيه للموضوع كما يعدم البصر في الموضوع وقتا من شأنه أن تكون له ملكة البصر. ولا وجود لهذا الشرط في قسمي التضاد فإن الموضوع المشترك للضدين اللذين لا واسطة بينهما يجوز في كل وقت أن ينتقل من أحدهما إلى الآخر، إلا أن يكون طبيعيا لا يفارق كبياض الققتس [؟]. وأيضًا يمكن في المتضادين أن يوجد الوسط دون الطرفين، ولا يمكن في العدم والملكة فإن في الحقيقي منه لا بد من أحدهما وفي المشهوري كذلك في الوقت. وأيضًا لا يلزم أن يكون أحد الضدين بين ارتفاع الآخر بخلاف العدم والملكة. وأما ما يكون بينهما وبين المشهوري على الخصوص أو بين الحقيقي كذلك فذلك يعرف بالتأمل بعد الإطلاق على كل واحد منهما. وكذلك ما يكون بين المتناقضين والمتضايفين فإنه في غاية الظهور بعد الاطلاع على حقيقة كل واحد منهما. وعلى هذا فيما يكون بينهما والعدم والملكة، وفيما يكون بين المتضايفين والعدم والملكة كذلك. واعلم أنا إذا قلنا عدم وملكة أو غير ذلك من المتقابلات فلسنا نشير منها إلا إلى طبائعها لا إليها من حيث وجودها للموضوع أو كون الموضوع متصفاً بها، فليس العمى وأن يعمى فالبصر وأن يبصر شيئًا واحدًا: ولهذا يقال زيد يعمى ولا يقال زيد عمى، وكون العمى لزيد معنى يقتضي نسبته للعمى إلى زيد. وأما العمى فهو معنى مفهوم بنفسه أو بسبب ما عدمه هو أعني البصر؛ إذ هو عدم للبصر، فهذه ليست المتقابلات الأول بل أمور تلحق المتقابلات فيعرض لها أن يكون مقابله. وعلى هذا في السلب والإيجاب فإن ما يوجب أو يُسلب نفسه ليس بقول بل هو محمول في القول كقولك جالس وليس بجالس. ثم العدم والملكة لا يكون أحدهما مقولاً بالنسبة إلى الآخر؛ أما الملكة فليست مفتقرة في تصورها إلى العدم البتة، وأما العدم كالعمى فإنه وإن كان لا يتصور إلا بتصور الملكة فإنه ليس مقول الماهية بالقياس إلى الملكة. وقد ظن بعض الناس أن العمى ينسب إلى البصر من طريق جنسه أو ما هو كجنسه وهو العدم. فإن العدم معقول بالعرض وبسبب ما هو عدمه: وهذا خطأ فإن العدم الذي هو جنس العمى ليس مقول الماهية بالقياس إلى شيء Commentary

Opposition of Good and Evil: Direct and Mediated
Analysis of opposition between good and evil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between cases where good directly opposes evil and cases where an intermediate good opposes two evil extremes, using the author's examples.

Core Idea
Not all goods oppose a single evil; some mediate between two vices.

This passage clarifies the logical relationships between opposites in moral categories. The author explains that while good and evil are generally opposites, in some cases a virtuous mean opposes two vicious extremes. Understanding this nuance is critical for correctly analyzing ethical and logical oppositions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of opposition mentioned
Read the first part of the passage and note how the author describes the opposition between good and evil absolutely, and between good and evil individually. Also look for the claim that evil can oppose evil in some cases.
The author uses 'illness-health' and 'injustice-justice' as examples of individual opposites.
2
Extract the definition of virtue as a median between extremes
Find where the author defines virtues as median dispositions between excess (ifrāṭ) and deficiency (tafrīṭ). Identify that the extremes are vices, and the middle virtue opposes both extremes.
Example: courage is a virtue between cowardice (deficiency) and recklessness (excess).
3
Distinguish between cases with a single opposite and cases with two opposites
Contrast the case of knowledge (good) vs ignorance (evil) where there is no intermediate good, with cases like courage where a good mediates two evils. Note the author's statement that the latter occurs only in few matters.
The author uses 'knowledge is good and ignorance is evil' as a paradigm case of direct opposition.
4
Analyze the author's correction of the misinterpretation about killing
Read the author's critique of the view that 'the middle in killing is bad'. The author argues that in justified contexts, killing can be good and not killing can be evil. This shows the complexity of determining good and evil in practical situations.
The example of 'killing in preserving the city' is from Islamic jurisprudence (siyasa).

فصل : [ فيما يتعلق بالتضاد من المباحث ] وما يتعلق بالتضاد من المباحث فذلك أهم بالنسبة إلى الغير؛ إذ فيه من الاختلافات بين الأهم كما قيل في الخير والشر إن الشر على الإطلاق ضد الخير على الإطلاق، وكل واحد من الشر لكل واحد من الخير كذلك كالمرض للصحة والجور للعدل فنحو ذلك . وأما مضادة الشر للشر فقد يكون؛ وذلك لأن الملكات المتوسطة بين الإفراط والتفريط في الأمور المتعلقة بالشهوة والغضب، وبالتدبير الجزئي في اقتناء الخير هي الفضائل والإفراطات والتفريطات هي الرذائل، فإن الجبن والتهور والخمود والفجور مثلا رذائل ؛ والوسائط تضاد الطرفين، وهذا إنما يوجد في قليل من الأمور. وأما في أكثر الأشياء فإن الخير يضاد الشر مطلقاً ولا يوجد للشر شر يضاده؛ فمن ذلك ما فيه الإفراط كله رديء كالجهل ، ومن ذلك أيضًا ما فيه الإفراط كله خير كالعلم. وقد قيل في قولهم وهذا إنما يوجد في قليل من الأمور أن المراد منه هو أن بعض الوسائط في الإفراطات والتفريطات ليس بخير مثل القتل فإن الوسط فيه رديء كله والطرف وهو اللا قتل خير كله؛ وليس المراد كذلك بل المراد أن من الشرور ما يوجد له خير يضاده وشر أيضًا يضاده. وذلك لأن هناك طبيعة موضوعة للإفراط والتفريط من أول حدود الإفراط إلى آخر حدود التفريط ذاهبًا باتصال واحد فهناك يوجد متوسط وطرفان في الطبع. ويكون المتوسط أيضًا هو خير يضاد الطرفين اللذين يضاد كل واحد منهما الخير؛ وهذا في قليل من الأمور؛ وليس الحكم في كل الأمور هكذا فإن العلم خير والجهل شر؛ وليس هناك توسط هو خير فطرفان هما شران . وكذلك الحال في كثير من الأشياء. وأما حديث القتل ففيه نظر لأن قتل من ينبغي قتله حين ينبغي على الوجه الذي ينبغي في خفظ المدينة مثلا هو من الخير كما أن ترك قتل من ينبغي قتله حين ينبغي على الوجه الذي ينبغي هو من الشر.
Section on what relates to contradiction from the investigations. What relates to contradiction from the investigations is most important relative to others; for in it are differences among the most important, as it is said about good and evil: Evil absolutely is the opposite of good absolutely, and each evil is opposite to each good likewise, like illness to health and injustice to justice, and so on. As for the opposition of evil to evil, it may occur; because the median dispositions between excess and deficiency in matters related to desire and anger, and in partial management in acquiring good, are virtues, and the excesses and deficiencies are vices. For example, cowardice, recklessness, lethargy, and debauchery are vices; and the intermediate oppose the two extremes, and this occurs only in few matters. As for most things, good opposes evil absolutely, and there is no evil opposing evil; among them is that in which all excess is bad, like ignorance, and also that in which all excess is good, like knowledge. It has been said regarding their statement 'and this occurs only in few matters' that what is meant is that some intermediates in excesses and deficiencies are not good, like killing, for the middle in it is entirely bad, and the extreme, which is not killing, is entirely good. But the meaning is not that; rather, the meaning is that among evils there is some for which there is a good opposing it and also an evil opposing it. Because there is a nature disposed for excess and deficiency from the first limit of excess to the last limit of deficiency, proceeding in one continuum, so there exists a middle and two extremes in nature. And the middle is also good, opposing the two extremes each of which opposes good; and this is in few matters. The judgment is not so in all things, for knowledge is good and ignorance is evil, and there is no intermediate that is good, so the two extremes are both evils. And the situation is similar in many things. As for the discussion of killing, it requires consideration, because killing one who ought to be killed at the time and in the manner that ought to be, for example, in preserving the city, is from good, just as refraining from killing one who ought to be killed at the time and in the manner that ought to be is from evil.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is a definitional exploration of the nature of opposition (تضاد) between good and evil. The author begins by stating that the investigation of contradiction is important due to its implications. He then explains that while good and evil are absolute opposites, evil can also oppose evil in certain cases. This occurs in the domain of moral dispositions where virtues (الفضائل) are median states between extremes (الإفراط والتفريط), which are vices (الرذائل). For instance, courage is a virtue situated between cowardice and recklessness, both vices. The median thus opposes both extremes. However, this is rare. In most cases, good directly opposes evil, and there is no evil opposing another evil, as with knowledge (good) and ignorance (evil). A clarification is given about the interpretation of 'few matters': some mistakenly think it means that certain intermediates (like killing) are not good; but the correct meaning is that some evils (like extremes) are opposed by both a good (the middle) and another evil (the other extreme). For example, in a continuum between excess and deficiency, the middle is good and opposes both extremes. However, this pattern is not universal; in some cases (like knowledge vs. ignorance), there is no intermediate good. The author then critiques the example of killing, arguing that killing in justified circumstances is good, while not killing when it is required is evil. Thus, the passage clarifies the nuanced relationship between opposites, distinguishing between cases where good opposes evil directly and cases where a good intermediate opposes two evil extremes.

Essential vs Accidental Opposition in Virtues
Author distinguishes essential vs accidental opposition using courage example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish essential from accidental opposition in a set of qualities using the criteria of intrinsic nature versus relational attribution.

Core Idea
Essential opposition is between extremes; accidental opposition arises from external relations like praise and blame.

In this passage, the author clarifies that courage is not the essential opposite of cowardice, but rather a middle between two vices. This distinction is crucial for properly understanding opposition in qualities, a key concept in the logic of definitions. We will learn to identify essential opposites by examining natures apart from subjects, and accidental opposites by considering states and relations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two perspectives the author introduces.
The author presents two ways to view dispositions: (1) considering their natures apart from subjects, and (2) considering them in relation to subjects and the states they produce.
These correspond to intrinsic and relational analysis.
2
Determine what constitutes essential opposition.
Essential opposition is between two extremes that succeed each other on the same subject, with a middle that does not oppose either. Here, cowardice and recklessness are essential opposites because they share the vice nature and are at opposite ends.
3
Apply the distinction to the courage example.
Courage is a middle between cowardice and recklessness. It does not oppose either essentially; it only appears opposite to cowardice when considered from the accidental perspective of moral evaluation (good vs evil).
This shows accidental opposition depends on relational attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد هذا فنقول ينبغي أن تعلم أن الخير ليس يضاد كل واحد من الشرين بالذات؛ إذ الشجاعة ليست تضاد الجبن من حيث هو جبن بل من حيث تشارك الجبن والتهور في كون كل واحد منهما رذيلة والشجاعة فضيلة؛ فإذن الضد بالذات للواحد واحد وإنما يحصل هذا بالنظر إلى هذه الملكات؛ وذلك على وجهين : أحدهما هو النظر في طبائعها ومعانيها غير مضافة إلى موضوعاتها من حيث إنها تفيد حالا لا يلزم لأجلها محمدة أو مذمة وهو أن ينظر في جملة الطبيعة التي بين الجبن والتهور مارا على الشجاعة من حيث هي ملكات يصدر عنها أفعالا ما؛ فحينئذ لا تكون الشجاعة مضادة لأحد الطرفين بل تكون أمرًا متوسطاً؛ فيكون الطرفان هما المتعاقبان على موضوع واحد وبينهما غاية البعد فيكونان هما الضدين فقط. والثاني هو النظر فيها من حيث الأحوال التي تحصل لموضوعاتها؛ وذلك باعتبار أنها أمور تناسب مصلحة نفس الإنسان أو نوعه أو لإنسانيته. وهذا باعتبار أمر يعرض للكيفيات من جهة إضافات لها؛ وليس في ذواتها كما أن كون الشيء حارا أو باردًا غير كونه موافقا وكون الجسم في طبيعته بحال غير كونه دواء نافعا أو شيئًا قابلا . وإذا اتضح ما قلناه فقد علمتَ أن الكيفية التي يقال لها جبن والتي يقال لها شجاعة لا يضادان في ذاتيهما بل من عارض سمي به أحدهما جبنا والآخر شجاعة ولا يضاد ذلك من حيث طبيعتها بل طبيعتها وسط. ثم إن ههنا أمورًا أخرى بينها متوسطات ولا يوجد المتوسط فيها مضادا لشيء من الطرفين؛ إذ ليست لها هذه النسبة، فإن الفاتر مثلا لا يضاد شيئًا
After this, we say: You should know that good does not oppose each of the two evils in essence. For courage does not oppose cowardice insofar as it is cowardice, but insofar as cowardice and recklessness share in each being a vice and courage is a virtue. Therefore, the opposite in essence is one for one, and this occurs only by considering these dispositions. And that is in two aspects: one is considering their natures and meanings without being added to their subjects, insofar as they convey a state for which no praise or blame necessarily follows, and that is to consider the entirety of the nature between cowardice and recklessness, passing through courage, insofar as they are dispositions from which certain actions proceed. Then courage is not opposite to either extreme but is a middle thing; thus the two extremes are the ones that succeed one another on one subject, and between them is utmost distance, so they alone are the two opposites. The second aspect is considering them in terms of the states that occur for their subjects; that is, considering that they are things suitable for the benefit of the human soul or its species or for its humanity. And this is due to something that occurs to qualities from the perspective of relations they have, not in their essences, just as a thing being hot or cold is not the same as it being agreeable, and a body being in a certain natural state is not the same as it being a beneficial medicine or something suitable. And when what we said is clear, you have known that the quality called cowardice and that called courage do not oppose each other in their essences, but rather from an accident one is named cowardice and the other courage, and they do not oppose in terms of their nature, but their nature is a middle. Then here are other things among which there are middles, and the middle does not oppose either of the extremes, because they do not have this relation; for example, tepid does not oppose anything.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage continues the definitional analysis of opposition, focusing on the distinction between essential (بالذات) and accidental opposition. The author states that good does not oppose each evil in essence. Using the example of courage, he explains that courage does not oppose cowardice essentially (since another extreme, recklessness, also exists), but rather because both cowardice and recklessness are vices and courage is a virtue. Thus, the essential opposite of one thing is only one, but here we have two extremes opposing each other. To clarify, two perspectives are given: (1) Consider the natures of the dispositions apart from their subjects. In this view, courage is simply a middle between cowardice and recklessness; it does not oppose either, but the two extremes (cowardice and recklessness) are opposites that succeed each other on the same subject. (2) Consider the dispositions in relation to their subjects and the beneficial or harmful states they produce. From this perspective, courage is considered good and cowardice evil, so they appear as opposites accidentally, not in their intrinsic natures. The author compares this to qualities like heat and cold: being hot or cold in essence is not the same as being agreeable or beneficial, which are accidental relations. Therefore, cowardice and courage do not oppose each other in essence; their natures are middle, and the accidental attribution of praise and blame makes them appear opposite. Finally, the author mentions other cases where the middle does not oppose either extreme, like tepid water, which is not opposite to hot or cold because it lacks that relation.

Tepid Water: An Intermediate Without Opposition
Author uses tepid water to illustrate intermediates that are not opposed to either extreme.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between intermediates that oppose their extremes and those that do not, using examples from Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
Not all intermediates oppose their extremes; some, like tepid water, are merely a blend.

In logic, opposition comes in different forms. This passage introduces a subtle but important type: intermediates that are not opposed to either extreme. By examining the example of tepid water, you will learn to recognize when a middle state is a mixture rather than a distinct opposite.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of intermediates
The passage contrasts two examples: courage (a mean between cowardice and recklessness) and tepid water (between hot and cold). Courage is a distinct state opposed to both extremes; tepid water is not.
Courage is a virtue that opposes both vices, while tepid water is simply a mixture.
2
Understand why tepid water does not oppose
Tepid water is composed of both hot and cold; it is not a separate quality that opposes them. It 'is the two extremes' in the sense of being a blend.
This contrasts with the usual mean, which is a unique state.
3
Locate the type of opposition involved
The author states that this kind of intermediate occurs only in contrariety (taḍād), not in privation/possession (ʿadam wa milka). In privation/possession, there is no intermediate.
For example, blind and seeing: there is no middle state.
4
Apply the concept to an Islamic science example
Consider the category of mubah (permissible) between wajib (obligatory) and haram (forbidden). Mubah is not opposed to either; it is a neutral permission. Similarly, in Islamic ethics, a balanced temperament (mizāj mutadil) is a blend of humors, not a separate opposite.
These examples help solidify the logical distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن ههنا أمورًا أخرى بينها متوسطات ولا يوجد المتوسط فيها مضادا لشيء من الطرفين؛ إذ ليست لها هذه النسبة، فإن الفاتر مثلا لا يضاد شيئًا خلط عن بل طرفاه. وإن كان حال الفاتر ليس كحال الشجاعة فإن الفاتر هو الطرفين بخلاف الشجاعة. ومع ذلك فإن هذه القسمة توجد في تقابل التضاد ولا توجد في تقابل العدم والملكة.
Then there are other things between which there are intermediates, and the intermediate in them is not opposed to anything of the two extremes, since it does not have this relation. For example, tepid water is not opposed to anything, but rather its two extremes (?). And although the case of tepid is not like the case of courage—for tepid is the two extremes, unlike courage—nevertheless this division exists in the opposition of contrariety and does not exist in the opposition of privation and possession.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
The passage introduces a second type of intermediate that does not oppose either extreme. Using the example of tepid water (al-fatir) between hot and cold, the author notes that tepid is not opposite to either; rather, it is the two extremes—i.e., it is a mixture of them. This contrasts with courage, which is a distinct intermediate between cowardice and recklessness but not identical to them. The author then distinguishes between two types of opposition: contrariety (taqābul al-taḍād) and privation/possession (taqābul al-'adam wa al-milka). The intermediate that is not opposed to either extreme only occurs in contrariety, not in privation/possession. In privation/possession, intermediates do not exist because the opposition is between having a quality and lacking it.

Distinguishing Opposites from Correlatives
Compares opposites and correlatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish opposites from correlatives based on whether one necessitates the existence of the other.

Core Idea
Opposites do not necessitate each other; correlatives do.

The author contrasts two types of relations: opposites (mutadaddān) and correlatives (mutadāyifān). Understanding this distinction is crucial for analyzing how terms relate in Islamic logic and theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of relations
Read the opening sentences to see that the author is comparing opposites (mutadaddān) and correlatives (mutadāyifān).
2
Compare the necessity condition
Notice that for opposites, the existence of one does not necessitate the other. For correlatives, it does. The author uses the example of 'all people healthy' vs. 'Zayd is healthy' to illustrate.
Consider the logical difference: absolute vs. particular statements.
3
Examine the correlative example
The author points out that a father can also be a son, showing that correlatives can coexist in one individual.
4
Formulate the distinction in your own words
Summarize: opposites are independent; correlatives are interdependent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد مرَّ من قبل في المتضادين أن وجود أحدهما مطلقا لا يوجب وجود الآخر لإيجاب المتضايفين؛ فإنا إذا توهمنا أن الناس كلهم صحياً لم يمتنع توهم ممارضته وجوب المرض. ولو قلنا زيد صحيح يمتنع أن يكون مريضًا؛ وهذا على خلاف ما يكون في المتضايفين فإن أحدهما مطلقا يوجب وجود الآخر، ولا يمتنع أن يكون ما هو أب هو أيضًا ابنا. ثم المحل في المتضايفين واحد فربما كان ذلك الواحد معنى أعم من نوع كالسواد والبياض فإن موضوعهما الجسم الطبيعي، وربما كان من نوع واحد مثل الجور والعدل فإن موضوعهما ليس كل نفس بل نفس إنسان. وربما كان الموضوع لضدين جنسًا كالعدد للزوجية والفردية مثلا، وربما كانا في جنس واحد كالسواد والبياض في اللون، وربما كانا في جنسين مختلفين كالعفة والفجور اللذين: أحدهما من جنس الفضيلة والآخر من جنس الرذيلة، وربما كانا في أنفسهما جنسين كالخير والشر. وبسبب أن يكون المعنى في قولهم إن الخير جنس»، ليس أنه مقول على الخير الجوهري والكمي والكيفي وغير ذلك بل من حيث هو مقول على الملكات فيكون متواطيا من هذا الوجه ثم إنه قد سومح في كونه ذاتيا / لها أو عرضيّاً لازما لهذه الملكات. فإن الحق أن الخير والشر يلزمها ولا يقومها. فإن كان ذلك كان الخير والشر من باب الكيف والمشهور أنهما من الأمور العامة للأشياء؛ وهذا من جملة ما يكون مفروعًا عنه في هذا الموضع فإن موضع التحقيق لهذه الأمور غير هذا الموضع. ومع ذلك فينبغي لنا أن نشير إشارة حقيقية فنقول إن الأضداد
It has already passed earlier concerning opposites that the existence of one of them absolutely does not necessitate the existence of the other, unlike correlatives. For if we imagine that all people are healthy, it is not impossible to imagine the necessity of sickness. But if we say Zayd is healthy, it is impossible that he be sick. This is contrary to what is the case with correlatives, for one of them absolutely necessitates the existence of the other, and it is not impossible that what is a father is also a son. Then the substrate in correlatives is one; so perhaps that one is a meaning more general than a species, like blackness and whiteness whose subject is natural body; and perhaps it is of one species, like injustice and justice whose subject is not every soul but the human soul. And the substrate for two opposites may be a genus, like number for evenness and oddness; and they may be in one genus, like blackness and whiteness in color; and they may be in two different genera, like chastity and debauchery, one of which is from the genus of virtue and the other from the genus of vice; and they may be in themselves two genera, like good and evil. And because the meaning in their saying that 'good is a genus' is not that it is predicated of essential good, quantitative good, qualitative good, etc., but insofar as it is predicated of dispositions, so it is univocal in this respect. Then it has been tolerated that it is essential to them or an inseparable accident for these dispositions. The truth is that good and evil are concomitant with them and do not constitute them. If that were the case, then good and evil would be from the category of quality, and it is well-known that they are among the general things. This is among what is set aside in this place, for the place of verification for these things is other than this place. Nevertheless, we should make a true indication and say: the opposites...
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage classifies types of opposites and distinguishes them from correlatives. The author first reiterates a previous point: in opposites (mutadaddān), the existence of one does not necessitate the existence of the other. For example, if we imagine all people are healthy, that does not necessitate sickness. But if we say Zayd is healthy, it prevents him from being sick simultaneously. This contrasts with correlatives (mutadāyifān), like father and son, where the existence of one necessitates the other, and the same individual can be both father and son. The author then discusses the substrate (maḥall) of opposites. In correlatives, the substrate is one (e.g., the same man can be father and son). In opposites, the substrate can vary: (a) a genus broader than species (e.g., natural body for blackness and whiteness); (b) a specific species (e.g., human soul for justice and injustice); (c) a genus (e.g., number for evenness and oddness); (d) the same genus (e.g., color for blackness and whiteness); (e) different genera (e.g., virtue and vice for chastity and debauchery); (f) themselves genera (e.g., good and evil). Finally, the author addresses a point about good and evil: they are not constitutive (qā'ima) of dispositions but concomitant (lāzima). They belong to the category of quality (kayf) but are general things. The author concedes that this is not the place for full investigation, but hints that opposites exist in various ways.

Key Terms
متضادان
متضايفان

A) Opposites have different substrates, correlatives have the same.
B) In opposites, one does not necessitate the existence of the other; in correlatives it does.
C) In opposites, one can be both simultaneously; in correlatives not.
D) Opposites are always in different genera.

Key Takeaway
The fundamental logical distinction between opposites and correlatives is the relation of necessity: opposites are independent, correlatives are interdependent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Give an example of a pair of opposites from the Quran (e.g., light and darkness) and explain why one does not necessitate the other.
?
Identify whether the pair 'iman' (faith) and 'kufr' (disbelief) are opposites or correlatives, and justify your answer using the author's criterion.

Classifying Substrates of Opposites
Classifies substrates of opposites

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the substrate of a given pair of opposites according to the six types discussed.

Core Idea
The substrate of opposites can be a genus, a species, or even a general accident.

After distinguishing opposites from correlatives, the author provides a detailed classification of the various types of substrates (mahall) in which opposites inhere. This classification helps in understanding how opposites can exist in different logical categories.

Guided Path
1
List the six types of substrates
From the passage, identify the six types: (a) more general than species (e.g., natural body for blackness/whiteness), (b) one species (e.g., human soul for justice/injustice), (c) a genus (e.g., number for evenness/oddness), (d) one genus (e.g., color for blackness/whiteness), (e) two different genera (e.g., virtue and vice for chastity/debauchery), (f) themselves genera (e.g., good and evil).
Note that some types overlap; pay attention to the examples.
2
Match each type with its example
For each type, look at the example given in the Arabic. Write them down.
3
Analyze the discussion on good and evil
The author notes that good and evil are not constitutive but concomitant, and they belong to the category of quality. This is a special case.
4
Apply the classification to a new pair
Try to classify a pair like 'knowledge and ignorance' using the author's scheme. What is their substrate? (Answer: they are in one genus - quality, or perhaps in the same species?)

It has already passed earlier concerning opposites that the existence of one of them absolutely does not necessitate the existence of the other, unlike correlatives. For if we imagine that all people are healthy, it is not impossible to imagine the necessity of sickness. But if we say Zayd is healthy, it is impossible that he be sick. This is contrary to what is the case with correlatives, for one of them absolutely necessitates the existence of the other, and it is not impossible that what is a father is also a son. Then the substrate in correlatives is one; so perhaps that one is a meaning more general than a species, like blackness and whiteness whose subject is natural body; and perhaps it is of one species, like injustice and justice whose subject is not every soul but the human soul. And the substrate for two opposites may be a genus, like number for evenness and oddness; and they may be in one genus, like blackness and whiteness in color; and they may be in two different genera, like chastity and debauchery, one of which is from the genus of virtue and the other from the genus of vice; and they may be in themselves two genera, like good and evil. And because the meaning in their saying that 'good is a genus' is not that it is predicated of essential good, quantitative good, qualitative good, etc., but insofar as it is predicated of dispositions, so it is univocal in this respect. Then it has been tolerated that it is essential to them or an inseparable accident for these dispositions. The truth is that good and evil are concomitant with them and do not constitute them. If that were the case, then good and evil would be from the category of quality, and it is well-known that they are among the general things. Commentary
This passage classifies types of opposites and distinguishes them from correlatives. The author first reiterates a previous point: in opposites (mutadaddān), the existence of one does not necessitate the existence of the other. For example, if we imagine all people are healthy, that does not necessitate sickness. But if we say Zayd is healthy, it prevents him from being sick simultaneously. This contrasts with correlatives (mutadāyifān), like father and son, where the existence of one necessitates the other, and the same individual can be both father and son. The author then discusses the substrate (maḥall) of opposites. In correlatives, the substrate is one (e.g., the same man can be father and son). In opposites, the substrate can vary: (a) a genus broader than species (e.g., natural body for blackness and whiteness); (b) a specific species (e.g., human soul for justice and injustice); (c) a genus (e.g., number for evenness and oddness); (d) the same genus (e.g., color for blackness and whiteness); (e) different genera (e.g., virtue and vice for chastity and debauchery); (f) themselves genera (e.g., good and evil). Finally, the author addresses a point about good and evil: they are not constitutive (qā'ima) of dispositions but concomitant (lāzima). They belong to the category of quality (kayf) but are general things. The author concedes that this is not the place for full investigation, but hints that opposites exist in various ways.
